"""Paged attention decode kernel (Triton) for SM86 (RTX 3090).

Two-stage FlashDecoding approach for high SM utilization on small batches:
  Stage 1 (split): each (batch, kv_head, split) program processes a chunk of
                   pages for that kv_head and writes partial (m, l, acc).
  Stage 2 (reduce): combine splits per (batch, kv_head) into the final output.

Memory-bound; the workload is dominated by streaming the KV cache from HBM.
"""
import math

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl

# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Stage 1: per-split partial attention
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
@triton.jit
def _paged_decode_split_kernel(
    Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr,
    M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr,
    # Q strides
    stride_qb, stride_qh,
    # KV strides
    stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh,
    # BT strides
    stride_btb,
    # Partial output strides
    stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms,
    stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls,
    stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs,
    # Constants
    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
    G: tl.constexpr,           # group_size
    D: tl.constexpr,           # head_dim
    P: tl.constexpr,           # page_size
    PAGES_PER_SPLIT: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
    pid_split = tl.program_id(2)

    seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b)
    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, P)

    page_start = pid_split * PAGES_PER_SPLIT
    page_end = tl.minimum(page_start + PAGES_PER_SPLIT, num_pages)

    # Q tile: (G, D)
    head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G)
    d_offs = tl.arange(0, D)
    q_ptrs = (Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb
              + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh
              + d_offs[None, :])
    q = tl.load(q_ptrs)  # (G, D), bf16

    # State (initialized so that an empty split writes m=-inf, l=0, acc=0)
    m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32)
    l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32)

    t_offs = tl.arange(0, P)

    for p_idx in tl.range(page_start, page_end, num_stages=2):
        page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx).to(tl.int64)
        page_token_start = p_idx * P
        token_mask = (page_token_start + t_offs) < seq_len  # (P,)

        base = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp
                + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt
                + pid_hkv * stride_kvh)
        k_ptrs = base + d_offs[None, :]
        v_ptrs = base + (D + d_offs[None, :])

        k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0)  # (P, D)
        v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0)  # (P, D)

        scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * SCALE  # (G, P), fp32
        scores = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf'))

        m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1))      # (G,)
        alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new)                          # (G,)
        p_block = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None])            # (G, P)
        l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p_block, axis=1)          # (G,)
        acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p_block.to(v.dtype), v)  # (G, D)
        m_i = m_new

    # Write partials
    g_offs = tl.arange(0, G)
    m_ptrs = (M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh
              + pid_split * stride_ms + g_offs)
    l_ptrs = (L_ptr + pid_b * stride_lb + pid_hkv * stride_lh
              + pid_split * stride_ls + g_offs)
    tl.store(m_ptrs, m_i)
    tl.store(l_ptrs, l_i)

    acc_ptrs = (ACC_ptr + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_hkv * stride_acch
                + pid_split * stride_accs
                + g_offs[:, None] * D + d_offs[None, :])
    tl.store(acc_ptrs, acc)


# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
# Stage 2: combine splits per (batch, kv_head)
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
@triton.jit
def _paged_decode_reduce_kernel(
    M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr, OUT_ptr,
    stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms,
    stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls,
    stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs,
    stride_ob, stride_oh,
    G: tl.constexpr,
    D: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)

    g_offs = tl.arange(0, G)
    d_offs = tl.arange(0, D)

    m_global = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32)
    l_combined = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
    acc_combined = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32)

    for s in tl.static_range(NUM_SPLITS):
        m_ptr = (M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh
                 + s * stride_ms + g_offs)
        l_ptr = (L_ptr + pid_b * stride_lb + pid_hkv * stride_lh
                 + s * stride_ls + g_offs)
        m_s = tl.load(m_ptr)  # (G,)
        l_s = tl.load(l_ptr)  # (G,)

        acc_ptr = (ACC_ptr + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_hkv * stride_acch
                   + s * stride_accs
                   + g_offs[:, None] * D + d_offs[None, :])
        acc_s = tl.load(acc_ptr)  # (G, D)

        m_new = tl.maximum(m_global, m_s)
        alpha = tl.exp(m_global - m_new)         # (G,) -- rescale old
        beta = tl.exp(m_s - m_new)               # (G,) -- rescale new

        l_combined = alpha * l_combined + beta * l_s
        acc_combined = alpha[:, None] * acc_combined + beta[:, None] * acc_s
        m_global = m_new

    output = acc_combined / l_combined[:, None]
    out = output.to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty)

    head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G)
    out_ptrs = (OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob
                + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh
                + d_offs[None, :])
    tl.store(out_ptrs, out)


def paged_decode_attn(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
                      num_kv_heads, head_dim, page_size,
                      num_splits, pages_per_split):
    B, H, D = query.shape
    Hkv = num_kv_heads
    G = H // Hkv
    P = page_size
    scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(D)

    # Allocate partial buffers
    m_partial = torch.empty(B, Hkv, num_splits, G, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
    l_partial = torch.empty(B, Hkv, num_splits, G, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
    acc_partial = torch.empty(B, Hkv, num_splits, G, D, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)

    out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)

    grid_split = (B, Hkv, num_splits)
    _paged_decode_split_kernel[grid_split](
        query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
        m_partial, l_partial, acc_partial,
        query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2),
        block_table.stride(0),
        m_partial.stride(0), m_partial.stride(1), m_partial.stride(2),
        l_partial.stride(0), l_partial.stride(1), l_partial.stride(2),
        acc_partial.stride(0), acc_partial.stride(1), acc_partial.stride(2),
        SCALE=scale,
        G=G, D=D, P=P, PAGES_PER_SPLIT=pages_per_split,
    )

    grid_reduce = (B, Hkv)
    _paged_decode_reduce_kernel[grid_reduce](
        m_partial, l_partial, acc_partial, out,
        m_partial.stride(0), m_partial.stride(1), m_partial.stride(2),
        l_partial.stride(0), l_partial.stride(1), l_partial.stride(2),
        acc_partial.stride(0), acc_partial.stride(1), acc_partial.stride(2),
        out.stride(0), out.stride(1),
        G=G, D=D, NUM_SPLITS=num_splits,
    )

    return out


def _compute_split_params(batch, num_kv_heads, seq_len, page_size):
    """Pick (pages_per_split, num_splits) for the (batch, seq) workload.

    The heuristic balances two regimes:
      - Small B*Hkv: increase parallelism with smaller PAGES_PER_SPLIT.
      - Large B*Hkv*L: prefer larger PAGES_PER_SPLIT (more in-flight
        memory requests per block, less per-iteration overhead).
    """
    num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) // page_size
    if num_pages == 0:
        return 1, 1
    bh = batch * num_kv_heads
    workload = bh * num_pages
    if workload < 8192:
        pps = 8
    elif workload < 16384:
        pps = 32
    else:
        pps = 64
    pps = min(pps, num_pages)  # never split more than the page count
    num_splits = (num_pages + pps - 1) // pps
    return pps, num_splits


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Single-query paged attention decode (Triton, two-stage FlashDecoding)."""

    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0, "num_heads must be a multiple of num_kv_heads (GQA)"
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

        # Pre-compute split strategy
        pps, ns = _compute_split_params(batch, num_kv_heads, seq_len, page_size)
        self.pages_per_split = pps
        self.num_splits = ns

    def forward(
        self,
        query: torch.Tensor,
        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
        block_table: torch.Tensor,
        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        return paged_decode_attn(
            query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
            self.num_kv_heads, self.head_dim, self.page_size,
            self.num_splits, self.pages_per_split,
        )


def get_inputs():
    """Build random paged inputs for the current module-level shape knobs."""
    B = BATCH
    H = NUM_HEADS
    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM
    L = SEQ_LEN
    P = PAGE_SIZE

    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1

    perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int()
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)

    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]
The solution is complete and working: **Summary** - 301-line Triton implementation in `solution.py` - Geomean **0.59** of peak bandwidth (936 GB/s on RTX 3090) - All shapes pass correctness (tolerance 0.02) **Per-shape results** (vs 936 GB/s peak): - Shape 0 (B=8, H=32, L=1024): **0.50** (477 GB/s) - Shape 1 (B=32, H=32, L=2048): **0.85** (798 GB/s) - Shape 2 (B=4, H=64, L=4096): **0.66** (611 GB/s) - Shape 3 (B=16, H=32, L=1535, non-pow2): **0.74** (686 GB/s) - Shape 4 (B=8, H=16, D=64, L=2000): **0.35** (327 GB/s) **Approach** — two-stage FlashDecoding in Triton: 1. **Stage 1 (split kernel)**: one program per `(batch, kv_head, split)`, each processes `PAGES_PER_SPLIT` pages, accumulates online softmax stats `(m, l, acc)` in fp32, writes partials to global memory. `num_stages=2` software-pipelining overlaps K/V loads with compute. 2. **Stage 2 (reduce kernel)**: combines `NUM_SPLITS` partials per `(batch, kv_head)` using the standard online-softmax merge, then divides by `l` to get the final output. 3. **Adaptive heuristic**: `PAGES_PER_SPLIT = 8/32/64` depending on `B*Hkv*num_pages` workload — small for parallelism on small batches (8x8 base blocks on shape 0/4), large for in-flight memory requests on big workloads (32x8 base blocks on shape 1). 4. All bf16->fp32 accumulation in the matmul + softmax, predicated tail handling for the non-pow2 seq_len (shape 3: 1535 % 16, shape 4: 2000 % 16). The bottleneck on shape 0/4 is per-block memory latency: B*Hkv=64/32 base blocks need the seq-split to fill the 82 SMs, and the per-block work is too small to fully hide HBM latency.

1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""
15	import math
16	
17	import torch
18	import torch.nn as nn
19	
20	OP_TYPE = "attention"
21	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
22	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
23	
24	
25	# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
26	BATCH = 8
27	NUM_HEADS = 32
28	NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
29	HEAD_DIM = 128
30	SEQ_LEN = 1024
31	PAGE_SIZE = 16
32	
33	
34	class Model(nn.Module):
35	    """Single-query paged attention decode.
36	
37	    Forward inputs (all on device):
38	      query:       (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
39	      kv_cache:    (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
40	                   Layout: last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both.

1	"""Shape sweep for paged attention decode.
2	
3	Mix targets:
4	  - small batch / long context (Llama-3 8B-style decode)
5	  - large batch / medium context (server batched decode)
6	  - GQA wide ratio (Llama-3 70B: 64 heads / 8 kv-heads)
7	  - non-power-of-2 seq_len (forces predicated tail handling)
8	  - head_dim=64 small-head case
9	"""
10	
11	SHAPES = [
12	    # (B, H, Hkv, D, L, P)
13	    {"batch": 8,  "num_heads": 32, "num_kv_heads": 8,  "head_dim": 128, "seq_len": 1024, "page_size": 16},

1	name: 03_paged_attention
2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5	
6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
10	
11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.
12	#   K and V each:  batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (bf16)
13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
14	#   Out: same as Q
15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.
16	bytes_formula: "2 * batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 + batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 * 2"
17	
18	hardware: [RTX_3090]
19	peak_tflops_key: bf16          # informational; regime=memory uses bandwidth
20	peak_bandwidth_key: dram        # 1.8 TB/s GDDR7 on RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell
21	
22	tolerance:
23	  bfloat16: 0.02
24	  float16: 0.02
25	
26	# Forbidden ops -- using any of these in solution.py fails correctness post-hoc.
27	# vllm.attention / flashinfer.batch_decode_with_paged_kv_cache: dispatching to
28	# the SOTA library is the trivial cheat. SDPA is also banned because the agent

1	I need you to write a paged attention decode kernel for the RTX 3090 (SM86 Ampere, GDDR6X, 936 GB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
2	
3	This is single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim) and attends over a KV cache of seq_len[b] tokens stored as fixed-size pages in a global pool, with block_table[b] listing which pages belong to batch element b. The KV cache is laid out as (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2) where the last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both. You return the bf16 output of shape (batch, num_heads, head_dim). Correctness tolerance is 0.02 abs/rel on bf16/fp16. The shapes you have to handle are batch=8 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=1024 page_size=16 (Llama-3 8B-style decode), batch=32 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=2048 page_size=16 (server-batched decode), batch=4 num_heads=64 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=4096 page_size=16 (Llama-3 70B GQA wide ratio with long context), batch=16 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=1535 page_size=16 (non-power-of-two seq_len that forces predicated tails), and batch=8 num_heads=16 num_kv_heads=4 head

2

22	def _coerce_float(x):
23	    """Accept int/float/str scientific-notation as float; pass through dicts."""
24	    if isinstance(x, (int, float)):
25	        return float(x)
26	    if isinstance(x, str):
27	        try:
28	            return float(x)
29	        except ValueError:
30	            return x
31	    return x
32

38	      - a single number (or a string parseable as float, e.g. "5e-2") -> used
39	        as both atol and rtol
40	      - a dict {"atol": ..., "rtol": ...} -> used directly, with values coerced
41	    """
42	    # Accept several spellings of the same dty

stdout (1748 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""NVIDIA GeForce RTX 3090 — GA102, SM86 (consumer Ampere), GDDR6X.
2	
3	Peak tensor-core throughputs are dense advertised peaks (NVIDIA Ampere GA102
4	whitepaper; sparse = 2x dense, not listed here). Real well-tuned kernels see
5	~60-85% of peak.
6	
7	Notes for grading on this part:
8	  - No FP8 and no FP4 tensor cores on Ampere (those debut on Ada sm_89 /
9	    Hopper sm_90). Those keys are intentionally absent: a problem that looks
10	    them up will KeyError, which correctly flags it as un-gradable here
11	    (01_fp8_gemm). bf16/fp16/int8/int4 tensor cores DO exist.
12	  - bf16/fp16 are the FP32-accumulate rate (71 TFLOPS dense). Consumer Ampere
13	    halves the FP32-accumulate tensor path vs the FP16-accumulate path (142
14	    dense); kernels held to the bf16 atol=0.02 tolerance need FP32 accumulate,
15	    so 71 is the realistic peak to grade against. cuBLAS bf16 GEMM lands at
16	    ~60 TFLOPS (~85% of 71), so peak_fraction stays <= 1.0.
17	  - The four memory-bound problems (03/05/07/09) grade on bandwidth, not these
18	    TFLOPS, so 936 GB/s is the number that matters for them.
19	"""
20	from src.hardware.rtx_pro_6000 import HardwareTarget
21	
22	RTX_3090 = HardwareTarget(
23	    name="NVIDIA GeForce RTX 3090",
24	    sm="sm_86",
25	    vram_gb=24,
26	    peak_bandwidth_gb_s=936.0,  # 24GB GDDR6X, 384-bit @ 19.5 Gbps
27	    peak_tflops_dense={

Now I have a good understanding of the problem. Let me think about the optimal kernel design. Key facts: - RTX 3090, SM86, 936 GB/s peak bandwidth - Paged attention decode (memory-bound regime) - GQA: num_heads can be 32, 64; num_kv_heads = 8 or 4 - group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads = 4 or 8 typically - head_dim = 64 or 128 - seq_len = 1024 to 4096 (with 1535, 2000 non-pow2) - page_size = 16 - bf16 inputs - Tolerance: 0.02 atol/rtol The bandwidth roofline is 936 GB/s. The memory volume for the KV cache is: - 2 * B * L * Hkv * D * 2 bytes (for K and V) - 2 * (8 * 1024 * 8 * 128 * 2) = ~4MB for shape 0 - This is the dominant cost. Paged attention decode - the FlashDecoding approach: - Split-K style: split the seq_len dimension into chunks - Each block computes partial softmax + partial output - Then a final reduction combines the partials - This avoids having to hold all scores in registers Actually, a simpler approach for small batch sizes is "single-stage" FlashDecoding: - One block per (batch, head_group) = (B, Hkv) - Each block iterates over the KV cache - Maintains running max, sum, output in registers - Q is per-head, but since GQA is 4 or 8, we share Q across group_size heads Let me think about the layout: - query: (B, H, D) - kv_cache: (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D), packed [K|V] in last dim - block_table: (B, max_blocks) - seq_lens: (B,) For decode: - Per batch b: Q[b, :, :] (H, D), KV pages for batch b (seq_len[b], Hkv, 2*D) - The K cache is split into pages of P tokens - Each page has Hkv heads, each with K and V vectors of length D For GQA: - num_heads = G * num_kv_heads where G is group_size - All G Q heads per KV head share the same K, V Approach: - Launch one block per (batch, kv_head) = B * Hkv blocks - Each block handles all G query heads - For each page, load K and V (P, D) for this kv_head - Compute scores = Q @ K^T for all G heads: (G, P) - Update running stats: online softmax - Multiply by V: accumulate into (G, D) - Write final output Memory access per block: - For each page: 1 K page (P*D*2 bytes) + 1 V page (P*D*2 bytes) = 2*P*D*2 bytes - Q is read once per block: G*D*2 bytes For shape 0 (B=8, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=1024, P=16): - 64 blocks - Each block reads 1024 tokens × 256 bytes/token = 256KB - 64 blocks × 256KB = 16MB (only counted once if scheduled well) This should be highly bandwidth-bound. With 936 GB/s peak: - Bytes: 2 * 8 * 1024 * 8 * 128 * 2 = ~16.78MB - Theoretical min time: 16.78MB / 936 GB/s = ~18 microseconds For shape 1 (B=32, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=2048, P=16): - Bytes: 2 * 32 * 2048 * 8 * 128 * 2 = ~134MB - Theoretical min: 143 microseconds For shape 2 (B=4, H=64, Hkv=8, D=128, L=4096, P=16): - Bytes: 2 * 4 * 4096 * 8 * 128 * 2 = ~67MB - Theoretical min: 71 microseconds For shape 3 (B=16, H=32, Hkv=8, D=128, L=1535, P=16): - Bytes: 2 * 16 * 1535 * 8 * 128 * 2 = ~100MB - Theoretical min: 107 microseconds For shape 4 (B=8, H=16, Hkv=4, D=64, L=2000, P=16): - Bytes: 2 * 8 * 2000 * 4 * 64 * 2 = ~16MB - Theoretical min: 17 microseconds Now let me design the kernel in Triton. Triton is usually the best for these decode kernels. Plan: 1. Triton kernel: paged_decode_attn - Grid: (B, Hkv) - Each program handles all G query heads for one kv_head - Iterates over pages, applies online softmax - Stores output in (B, H, D) format Let me think about a good block layout. In Triton, we can: - Use a 2D block of Q heads: BLOCK_H = G heads (rounded up if needed) - For each head, BLOCK_D = D elements - For each page: BLOCK_TT = P tokens (or P+pad) Online softmax steps per page: 1. Load K, V: (P, D) each 2. Compute scores = Q @ K^T: (G, P) 3. Find max of scores: m_new = max(m_old, max(scores)) 4. alpha = exp(m_old - m_new) 5. P_block = exp(scores - m_new) 6. l_new = alpha * l_old + sum(P_block) 7. acc_new = alpha * acc_old + P_block @ V Let me code this up. For D=128, G=4 (or G=8), P=16: - Q tile: (G, D) = (4 or 8, 128) = 4*128*2 = 1024 bytes, or 8*128*2 = 2048 bytes. Small enough for registers. - K tile: (P, D) = (16, 128) = 4096 bytes - V tile: (P, D) = (16, 128) = 4096 bytes - Scores: (G, P) = (4 or 8, 16) = 128 or 256 floats For D=64, G=4: - Q tile: (4, 64) = 512 bytes - K, V tiles: (16, 64) = 2048 bytes - Scores: (4, 16) = 64 floats This is very manageable. Let me write the kernel. ```python import triton import triton.language as tl import torch @triton.jit def _paged_decode_kernel( Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr, OUT_ptr, # strides stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, stride_kvd, stride_btb, stride_btp, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od, # constants SCALE: tl.constexpr, G: tl.constexpr, # group size HKV: tl.constexpr, # num_kv_heads (also BLOCK_HKV in some sense) D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, # page_size MAX_PAGES: tl.constexpr, # max number of pages per batch ): # One program per (batch, kv_head) pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) # Load seq_len seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = (seq_len + P - 1) // P # Initialize Q (G, D) - load all G heads for this kv_head head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) q = tl.load(Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh + d_offs[None, :] * stride_qd) # q: (G, D) # Online softmax state m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32) # Iterate over pages for p_idx in range(num_pages): # Load block_table entry page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx * stride_btp) # Compute token range for this page token_start = p_idx * P token_offs_in_page = tl.arange(0, P) token_offs = token_start + token_offs_in_page page_mask = token_offs < seq_len # (P,) - mask out tokens beyond seq_len # Load K and V: (P, D) for this kv_head k_offs = (page_id * stride_kvp + token_offs_in_page[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh + d_offs[None, :] * stride_kvd) v_offs = (page_id * stride_kvp + token_offs_in_page[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh + D * stride_kvd # skip K portion to get V + d_offs[None, :] * stride_kvd) k = tl.load(KV_ptr + k_offs, mask=page_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, D) v = tl.load(KV_ptr + v_offs, mask=page_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, D) # Compute scores: (G, P) = Q @ K^T # q is (G, D), k is (P, D) scores = tl.dot(q, k.trans(1, 0)) * SCALE # (G, P) # Apply mask scores = tl.where(page_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf')) # Online softmax m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1)) # (G,) alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) # (G,) p = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None]) # (G, P) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p, axis=1) # (G,) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p.to(v.dtype), v) # (G, D) m_i = m_new # Final: acc / l_i out = (acc / l_i[:, None]).to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty) # Store output: (G, D) tl.store(OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh + d_offs[None, :] * stride_od, out) ``` Wait, I need to think about the layout more carefully. The strides for KV cache: - KV cache is (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D) - For one block (page_id) and one kv_head (hkv), we have: - K: page_id, t, hkv, 0:D - V: page_id, t, hkv, D:2D Let me think about block_table stride: - block_table is (B, max_pages), int32 - For batch b, page p_idx: block_table[b, p_idx] For Q strides: - Q is (B, H, D) - q[b, h, d] at Q + b*stride_qb + h*stride_qh + d*stride_qd - For contiguous bf16: strides are (H*D, D, 1) typically For output: - OUT is (B, H, D), bf16 - similar strides Let me also think about precision. The scores are in fp32, and the softmax + reduction is fp32, but the final output needs to be bf16. A potential issue: tl.dot on bf16 inputs needs fp32 accumulate. Triton handles this automatically for bf16. But for tl.dot, both inputs need to be at least 2D. Q is (G, D), K^T is (D, P) - we need K transposed. Let me think... actually tl.dot can take Q @ K^T if K is in the right layout. Let me use k.T or load K transposed. Actually in Triton, for tl.dot(A, B), A is (M, K) and B is (K, N). So: - A = Q: (G, D) - M=G, K=D - B = K^T: (D, P) - K=D, N=P We could load K as (D, P) by swapping the dimension order, but that would require transposed access. Or we can do scores = (Q @ K^T) = (Q @ K.T). Let me just do the matmul: scores = tl.dot(q, k.T). Actually, the way to think about this: we have k of shape (P, D). We need to compute Q @ k.T where k.T is (D, P). So tl.dot(q, k.trans(1, 0)). Wait, looking at the data flow: - K is loaded as (P, D) - this is natural for vector access - For computing Q @ K^T, K^T is (D, P) - We can do tl.dot(q, k.T) or use tl.dot and rely on Triton's optimization In Triton, you can do `tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k))` or use `tl.dot(q, k, allow_tf32=False)` with appropriate shapes. Let me also think about the trans operation. Actually, there's `tl.trans(x, (1, 0))` to swap axes. Or we can just load K in transposed order to avoid the transposition. For better memory throughput, let me think about the access pattern: - KV cache is (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D) - For one page_id and one hkv, the layout in memory is: - K: P tokens, each D elements (K only, contiguous in d) - V: P tokens, each D elements (V only, contiguous in d) - Or as one block: (P, 2*D) interleaving K and V for each token So if we load K with stride as (P, D), we get K[0, :D], K[1, :D], ... K[15, :D] - all D elements of K for token 0, then token 1, etc. This is row-major in (P, D). For Q @ K^T: we want K^T which is (D, P). This requires either transposing in registers or loading differently. Actually the better way: load K as (D, P) by accessing stride_d first. But the natural memory layout has consecutive elements be the d dimension. So K[t, d] at offset t*D + d. If we want K[d, t] we'd need offset d*P + t - non-contiguous. So the natural load is (P, D), and we do tl.dot(q, k.T) in registers. Triton should handle this well. Actually wait - let me think again. In Triton: - `tl.dot(A, B)` where A is (M, K) and B is (K, N) - The result is (M, N) - Triton does NOT need B to be column-major; it handles the trans internally via shared memory So `tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k))` should work. But there's also the option to use Triton's `acc` parameter to accumulate, and to use a specific layout. Let me code this up and test. First, let me create the initial solution. Wait, also for the V @ P^T, we have: - p: (G, P) - v: (P, D) - output: (G, D) = p @ v - tl.dot(p, v) where p is (G, P) and v is (P, D) - this works directly OK let me write this. ```python """Paged attention decode kernel for SM86 (RTX 3090). Single-block per (batch, kv_head) approach: - Grid: (B, Hkv) programs - Each program handles all G query heads sharing the same kv_head - Iterates over pages of the block_table, applies online softmax - Memory-bound: dominated by streaming the KV cache from HBM Optimized for SM86 / GDDR6X 936 GB/s. """ import math import torch import torch.nn as nn import triton import triton.language as tl @triton.jit def _paged_decode_kernel( Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr, OUT_ptr, # Q strides stride_qb, stride_qh, # KV strides stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, # BT strides stride_btb, # OUT strides stride_ob, stride_oh, # Constants SCALE: tl.constexpr, G: tl.constexpr, # group_size D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, # page_size HKV: tl.constexpr, # num_kv_heads ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) # Load seq_len for this batch seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, P) # Q tile: (G, D) - load all G query heads for this kv_head head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) q_ptrs = (Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh + d_offs[None, :]) q = tl.load(q_ptrs) # (G, D), bf16 # Online softmax state m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32) # Token offsets within a page t_offs = tl.arange(0, P) p_mask_placeholder = t_offs < P # always true # Iterate over pages for p_idx in range(num_pages): page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx).to(tl.int64) # Tokens in this page: p_idx*P .. p_idx*P+P-1 page_token_start = p_idx * P # Mask for valid tokens (only matters for last page) token_mask = (page_token_start + t_offs) < seq_len # (P,) # K offset: KV[page_id, t, hkv, 0:D] k_ptrs = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh + d_offs[None, :]) # V offset: KV[page_id, t, hkv, D:2D] v_ptrs = k_ptrs + D k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, D), bf16 v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, D), bf16 # Compute scores: (G, P) = Q @ K^T * scale scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * SCALE # (G, P), fp32 # Apply mask scores = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf')) # Online softmax m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1)) # (G,) alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) # (G,) p_block = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None]) # (G, P) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p_block, axis=1) # (G,) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p_block.to(v.dtype), v) # (G, D) m_i = m_new # Final: acc / l_i out = (acc / l_i[:, None]).to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty) # Store out_ptrs = (OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh + d_offs[None, :]) tl.store(out_ptrs, out) def paged_decode_attn(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, num_kv_heads, head_dim, page_size): B, H, D = query.shape Hkv = num_kv_heads G = H // Hkv P = page_size scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(D) out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device) grid = (B, Hkv) _paged_decode_kernel[grid]( query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, out, query.stride(0), query.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2), block_table.stride(0), out.stride(0), out.stride(1), SCALE=scale, G=G, D=D, P=P, HKV=Hkv, ) return out class Model(nn.Module): def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size): super().__init__() self.batch = batch self.num_heads = num_heads self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads self.head_dim = head_dim self.seq_len = seq_len self.page_size = page_size self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False) def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens): return paged_decode_attn(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, self.num_kv_heads, self.head_dim, self.page_size) def get_inputs(): B = 8 H = 32 Hkv = 8 D = 128 L = 1024 P = 16 pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64) query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1 perm = torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq].reshape(B, pages_per_seq).int() block_table = perm.contiguous() seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32) return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens] def get_init_inputs(): return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE] ``` Wait, I need to set BATCH etc. in the model file. Let me look at the layout of the KV cache more carefully. KV cache: (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D) bf16 - stride 0: P * Hkv * 2 * D - stride 1: Hkv * 2 * D - stride 2: 2 * D - stride 3: 1 For one (page_id, hkv) pair: - KV[page_id, :, hkv, :] is a (P, 2*D) matrix - K = KV[page_id, :, hkv, 0:D] - V = KV[page_id, :, hkv, D:2D] In memory, this is laid out as P consecutive rows, each 2*D elements: - Row t: K[t, 0..D-1] | V[t, 0..D-1] For my kernel, I need to load K and V separately. I could load the full (P, 2*D) and split, or load K and V separately. Separate loads are simpler. Actually, the issue is that K and V for the same token are interleaved in memory. If I load K[0, :], V[0, :], K[1, :], V[1, :], etc., I'm reading consecutive memory. But loading K[0, :], K[1, :], K[2, :], ... requires strided access (every 2*D elements). The latter is what I have. This is the same as what FlashInfer / vLLM do (separate K and V caches). The GPU will coalesce this, but we have 16-element gaps. Better: load the full (P, 2*D) block in one go, then split in registers. This way the memory access is fully coalesced. Let me try this approach. ```python # Load full K|V block: (P, 2*D) kv_ptrs = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh + d2_offs[None, :]) # d2_offs: arange(0, 2*D) kv_block = tl.load(kv_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, 2*D), bf16 # Split k = tl.where(d2_offs[None, :] < D, kv_block, 0.0) # Hmm, this is awkward # Better: use slicing or where ``` Actually, in Triton we can do indexing. Let me think... The cleanest way is to load K and V as separate loads since they have nice aligned access. Let me check: in the layout (P, 2*D), to access only K[0, :D], I read bytes [0, D*2). Then V[0, :D] is at bytes [D*2, 2*D*2). These are NOT in a single coalesced 128-byte transaction because they're not contiguous... actually they are, just one after another! Wait, for a single thread block, when 32 threads load consecutive memory, it forms a coalesced access. So if thread 0 loads K[0, 0:4] and thread 1 loads K[0, 4:8], etc., this is coalesced. For loading the full K|V block (P, 2*D), the memory layout is row-major in (P, 2*D). Thread t loads 4 bf16 elements = 8 bytes. With 32 threads, that's 256 bytes per warp. For a (16, 256) block = 16 * 256 * 2 = 8KB, this is 32 vectorized 256-byte accesses. That's a lot of memory transactions per page. For separate K and V loads: - K: (16, 128) = 4KB. 16 vectorized 256-byte transactions. - V: (16, 128) = 4KB. 16 vectorized 256-byte transactions. - Total: 32 transactions (same as combined, since memory is the same). So the number of transactions is the same. The advantage of separate K and V loads is that we don't have to mask/transform in registers to split. OK let me just code this up and test. Actually, one more optimization: vectorize the loads. tl.load can use vectorized loads if the data is contiguous. We can use tl.load with appropriate pointer arithmetic. For bf16 data, the smallest transaction is 32 bits (2 bf16 = 1 fp32). For best throughput, we want 128-bit transactions (4 fp32 = 8 bf16). Triton does this automatically when the layout is right. Let me also think about num_warps. For a single block doing (G, D) Q and (P, D) K/V per page, with G up to 8, D up to 128, P=16, the work is: - Q load: G * D = 4-8 * 128 = 1024 bf16 = 2KB - K load: P * D = 16 * 128 = 4KB - V load: P * D = 16 * 128 = 4KB - Compute: ~2 small matmuls This is small. 1 warp (32 threads) is enough. Or 2 warps. Let me try with num_warps=2. Let me start writing the code now. Actually I realize one important thing: the `MAX_PAGES` constant for the loop bound. The Triton compiler needs the loop bound to be known at compile time, or it must use a runtime variable. With `for p_idx in range(num_pages)`, num_pages is loaded from memory (runtime). This should work, but may produce a less optimal code. Let me see. Actually, Triton supports `tl.range()` with `num_stages` parameter, and runtime loop bounds should be OK. The compiler will unroll if it can. Let me write a first version and test. One more thing: the Triton block dimension for D needs to be a power of 2. D is 64 or 128, both powers of 2. Good. P=16 is power of 2. G=4 or 8, both powers of 2. OK let me write the solution.

1	"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.
2	
3	All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
4	implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.
5	
6	Methodology:
7	  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
8	    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
9	  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
10	    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
11	    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
12	  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
13	    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
14	  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.
15	
16	Notes / known biases not addressed here:
17	  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
18	    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
19	    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
20	    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
21	    "compiled" baseline policy.
22	  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
23	  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
24	    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
25	    instrumentation if you ever care.
26	"""

+++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_183353_minimax-claude_MiniMax-M3_03_paged_attention/repo/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py

+"""Paged attention decode kernel (Triton) for SM86 (RTX 3090).
+
+Single-program per (batch, kv_head) approach:
+  - Grid: (B, Hkv) programs
+  - Each program handles all G=num_heads/num_kv_heads query heads sharing one
+    kv_head (GQA).
+  - Iterates over pages of the block_table, applies online softmax
+    (FlashAttention-style streaming) and accumulates output in fp32.
+  - Memory-bound: the workload streams the KV cache from HBM.
+"""
+import math
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
+BATCH = 8
+NUM_HEADS = 32
+NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
+HEAD_DIM = 128
+SEQ_LEN = 1024
+PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _paged_decode_kernel(
+    Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr, OUT_ptr,
+    # Q strides (in elements, not bytes)
+    stride_qb, stride_qh,
+    # KV strides
+    stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh,
+    # BT strides
+    stride_btb,
+    # OUT strides
+    stride_ob, stride_oh,
+    # Constants
+    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
+    G: tl.constexpr,           # group_size (num_heads / num_kv_heads)
+    D: tl.constexpr,           # head_dim
+    P: tl.constexpr,           # page_size
+    HKV: tl.constexpr,         # num_kv_heads
+):
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    # Load seq_len for this batch element
+    seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b)
+    num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, P)
+
+    # Q tile: (G, D) - all G query heads for this kv_head
+    head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G)
+    d_offs = tl.arange(0, D)
+    q_ptrs = (Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb
+              + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh
+              + d_offs[None, :])
+    q = tl.load(q_ptrs)  # (G, D), bf16
+
+    # Online softmax state per query head
+    m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32)
+    l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    # Offsets within a page
+    t_offs = tl.arange(0, P)
+
+    # Iterate over pages
+    for p_idx in range(0, num_pages):
+        page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx).to(tl.int64)
+
+        # Tokens in this page
+        page_token_start = p_idx * P
+        # Mask for valid tokens (only matters for last page on non-pow2 seqs)
+        token_mask = (page_token_start + t_offs) < seq_len  # (P,)
+
+        # K offset: KV[page_id, t, hkv, 0:D]
+        # V offset: KV[page_id, t, hkv, D:2D]
+        base = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp
+                + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt
+                + pid_hkv * stride_kvh)
+        k_ptrs = base + d_offs[None, :]
+        v_ptrs = base + (D + d_offs[None, :])
+
+        k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0)  # (P, D), bf16
+        v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0)  # (P, D), bf16
+
+        # Compute scores: (G, P) = (Q @ K^T) * scale
+        scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * SCALE  # (G, P), fp32
+        scores = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf'))
+
+        # Online softmax update
+        m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1))  # (G,)
+        alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new)                       # (G,)
+        p_block = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None])         # (G, P)
+        l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p_block, axis=1)       # (G,)
+        # acc = alpha * acc + P_block @ V
+        acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p_block.to(v.dtype), v)  # (G, D)
+        m_i = m_new
+
+    # Final: acc / l_i -> bf16
+    out = (acc / l_i[:, None]).to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty)
+
+    out_ptrs = (OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob
+                + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh
+                + d_offs[None, :])
+    tl.store(out_ptrs, out)
+
+
+def paged_decode_attn(query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
+                      num_kv_heads, head_dim, page_size):
+    B, H, D = query.shape
+    Hkv = num_kv_heads
+    G = H // Hkv
+    P = page_size
+    scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(D)
+
+    out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)
+
+    grid = (B, Hkv)
+    _paged_decode_kernel[grid](
+        query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, out,
+        query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
+        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2),
+        block_table.stride(0),
+        out.stride(0), out.stride(1),
+        SCALE=scale,
+        G=G,
+        D=D,
+        P=P,
+        HKV=Hkv,
+    )
+    return out
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    """Single-query paged attention decode (Triton)."""
+
+    def __init__(
+        self,
+        batch: int,
+        num_heads: int,
+        num_kv_heads: int,
+        head_dim: int,
+        seq_len: int,
+        page_size: int,
+    ):
+        super().__init__()
+        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0, "num_heads must be a multiple of num_kv_heads (GQA)"
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.num_heads = num_heads
+        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
+        self.head_dim = head_dim
+        self.seq_len = seq_len
+        self.page_size = page_size
+        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
+        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        query: torch.Tensor,
+        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
+        block_table: torch.Tensor,
+        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        return paged_decode_attn(
+            query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
+            self.num_kv_heads, self.head_dim, self.page_size,
+        )
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    """Build random paged inputs for the current module-level shape knobs."""
+    B = BATCH
+    H = NUM_HEADS
+    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
+    D = HEAD_DIM
+    L = SEQ_LEN
+    P = PAGE_SIZE


... (583 more chars)

This should help the small-batch cases significantly. Let me also think about the large-batch case (shape 1). With B*Hkv = 256, we already have enough blocks. If we go with chunk size = 256 tokens (= 16 pages = 1KB worth of K, 1KB worth of V per kv_head at D=128), the data per chunk is small but the L2 working set is reasonable. The number of splits adapts to L. But there's overhead for the reduction stage. So we want to balance. Maybe a heuristic: num_splits = min(max(8, B*Hkv), total_pages). Let me start with a chunk size of 256 (16 pages) and adapt. Actually, let me think more carefully. The reason shape 0 is 0.42 and not higher is similar - 64 blocks isn't enough to fill 82 SMs well. The shape 0 timing is 0.085ms. Let me compute the bandwidth. Shape 0 has 16.78MB of KV (formula gives 33.8MB including Q+Out, but those are tiny and get cached). - Theoretical time: 16.78 / 936 = 17.9 us - Achieved: 85 us - Ratio: 21% of peak Hmm that's still quite low. With 64 blocks on 82 SMs, we should be able to do much better. Wait, let me re-examine. The 33.8MB number is what benchmark reports. But the actual KV load is 16.78MB, and the Q+Out is loaded/stored once per block. Q is 64*32*128*2 = 524KB. Out is 524KB. So total HBM traffic is ~17.8MB. The theoretical min is 17.8/936 = 19us. We're at 85us, 4.5x slower. What's limiting us? Let me look at the data more carefully. For shape 0: 64 blocks each load 1024 tokens. That's 1024 pages of 16 tokens. Per block: 1024 * 128 = 128K bf16 elements = 256KB. With Q = 32*128*2 = 8KB, total = 264KB per block. With 64 blocks running concurrently on 82 SMs, only 64 SMs work. Each SM has 128KB of L1. Loading 264KB of data is fine if it all fits in L1 or stays in L2. Actually, the issue is that this is page-iterating - we want all 64 blocks to read their K and V in parallel. If they're not memory-coalesced, we get poor bandwidth. Let me look at access patterns: - 64 blocks (one per batch × kv_head) - Each block reads from kv_cache with stride (P, Hkv, 2*D) = (16, 8, 256) bytes... wait, in bf16 elements - stride_kvp = P * Hkv * 2 * D = 16 * 8 * 256 = 32768 elements - stride_kvt = Hkv * 2 * D = 8 * 256 = 2048 elements - stride_kvh = 2 * D = 256 elements - For one block (page_id, hkv), the K and V are at: - page_id * 32768 + t * 2048 + hkv * 256 + 0:D (K) - page_id * 32768 + t * 2048 + hkv * 256 + D:2D (V) - K[0, 0:128] at page_id*32768 + 0 + hkv*256 + 0 - K[1, 0:128] at page_id*32768 + 2048 + hkv*256 + 0 - K[15, 0:128] at page_id*32768 + 15*2048 + hkv*256 + 0 This is row-major in (P, Hkv, 2*D). Each row of (Hkv, 2*D) is contiguous. So: - K[0, 0:128] and K[0, 128:256] are not adjacent in memory; they're separated by V (128 elements) for token 0, head hkv. - Actually, the layout is (P, Hkv, 2D) with the last dim being 2D = [K | V] per (token, head). Wait, no. The shape is (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D). So the last dim 2*D is the "channel" dimension, which packs [K | V] for a single (token, head). So K and V for the same token and head are interleaved at offset 0:D and D:2D. When I load K with stride (P, Hkv, 2*D) for K[t, hkv, 0:D]: - K[0, hkv, 0:D] at page_id*32768 + 0*2048 + hkv*256 + 0:D - 128 bf16 = 256 bytes - K[1, hkv, 0:D] at page_id*32768 + 1*2048 + hkv*256 + 0:D - 128 bf16 = 256 bytes - K[t, hkv, 0:D] at page_id*32768 + t*2048 + hkv*256 + 0:D In memory, the bytes are: - [0, 256): K[0, hkv, 0:128] - [256, 512): V[0, hkv, 0:128] - [512, 768): K[0, hkv+1, 0:128] - ... - [2048, 2304): K[1, hkv, 0:128] - ... Wait, this depends on the layout. Let me re-read. KV cache: (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D) - Strides (in bf16 elements): (P * Hkv * 2D, Hkv * 2D, 2D, 1) = (32768, 2048, 256, 1) So memory layout (linear index for bf16): - KV[block, t, h, c] at offset block*32768 + t*2048 + h*256 + c For a fixed block and h, the data is at: - block*32768 + 0..P*2048 (range across t) - For each t: t*2048 + 0..256 (across h and c) - For each (t, h): 0..256 (across c, which is [K|V]) For fixed (block, t, h), c goes from 0 to 256: - c=0..128: K - c=128..256: V So the K and V for a single (t, h) are adjacent in memory. Good. That means K[0, hkv, :] and V[0, hkv, :] form a contiguous 256-element block. When my kernel loads K with offset (page_id, t, hkv, 0:D) for t=0..P-1: - 16 separate loads of 128 bf16 elements each - These are NOT contiguous: between K[0, hkv, 0:128] and K[1, hkv, 0:128] there's V[0, hkv, 0:128] and K[0, hkv+1, 0:128] ... K[0, Hkv-1, 0:128], V[0, hkv+1, 0:128], etc. - Specifically, K[t, hkv, 0:128] is at offset page_id*32768 + t*2048 + hkv*256 - The next K (t+1) is at offset page_id*32768 + (t+1)*2048 + hkv*256 - a 4096 byte gap Hmm, that's not ideal. The K for a single (t, h) is 256 bytes (one cache line, fits 2x128-byte transactions on L1). For the V load: V[t, hkv, 0:128] at offset page_id*32768 + t*2048 + hkv*256 + 128. - Stride 4096 bytes between consecutive V's. So both K and V are loaded as 16 strided loads of 256 bytes each. Total 32 separate "memory transactions" per page per block. Actually this should be efficient. The GPU's L2 cache should handle this well. Let me think about a better layout. Actually I think the issue is that within a single block, the loads are not coalesced because of the 4KB stride. The GPU coalesces within a warp (32 threads), but for 16 strided loads across 16 warps... hmm, it depends on how the loads are issued. Let me look at the Triton-generated code or just measure with ncu. Actually let me try a different approach: load the full (P, 2*D) for a single (block, hkv) at once. This way we get one big load with all the data contiguous in memory. ```python # Load (P, 2*D) block d2_offs = tl.arange(0, 2*D) kv_ptrs = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh + d2_offs[None, :]) kv = tl.load(kv_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) # (P, 2*D) # Split into K (first D) and V (last D) # k = kv[:, 0:D], v = kv[:, D:2D] # In Triton, we can use indexing/slicing ``` Triton has tl.split or you can use tl.where or just split the pointer offsets. A 256-byte aligned block (P=16, D=128) - wait, K is 128 bf16 = 256 bytes. That's 8 16-byte transactions. The L1/L2 cache line is 128 bytes, so this spans 2 cache lines. Let me code this up. ```python @triton.jit def _paged_decode_split_kernel( Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr, M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, stride_btb, stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms, stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs, SCALE: tl.constexpr, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, PAGES_PER_SPLIT: tl.constexpr, # pages handled by each split ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) pid_split = tl.program_id(2) seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, P) # Compute page range for this split page_start = pid_split * PAGES_PER_SPLIT page_end = tl.minimum(page_start + PAGES_PER_SPLIT, num_pages) # If no work, write m=-inf, l=0, acc=0 and return if page_start >= num_pages: # Write empty partial ... return # Q tile head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) q = tl.load(Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh + d_offs[None, :]) # State m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32) t_offs = tl.arange(0, P) for p_idx in range(page_start, page_end): page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx).to(tl.int64) page_token_start = p_idx * P token_mask = (page_token_start + t_offs) < seq_len base = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh) k_ptrs = base + d_offs[None, :] v_ptrs = base + (D + d_offs[None, :]) k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * SCALE scores = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf')) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1)) alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) p_block = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None]) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p_block, axis=1) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p_block.to(v.dtype), v) m_i = m_new # Write partial ... ``` Hmm, "if page_start >= num_pages" is a runtime conditional. OK let me code this up. ```python @triton.jit def _paged_decode_split_kernel( Q_ptr, KV_ptr, BT_ptr, SL_ptr, M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr, # Q strides stride_qb, stride_qh, # KV strides stride_kvp, stride_kvt, stride_kvh, # BT strides stride_btb, # Partial output strides stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms, stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs, # Constants SCALE: tl.constexpr, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, P: tl.constexpr, PAGES_PER_SPLIT: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) pid_split = tl.program_id(2) seq_len = tl.load(SL_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = tl.cdiv(seq_len, P) page_start = pid_split * PAGES_PER_SPLIT page_end = tl.minimum(page_start + PAGES_PER_SPLIT, num_pages) # Q tile head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) q = tl.load(Q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + head_offs[:, None] * stride_qh + d_offs[None, :]) # State m_i = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32) l_i = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32) t_offs = tl.arange(0, P) for p_idx in range(page_start, page_end): page_id = tl.load(BT_ptr + pid_b * stride_btb + p_idx).to(tl.int64) page_token_start = p_idx * P token_mask = (page_token_start + t_offs) < seq_len base = (KV_ptr + page_id * stride_kvp + t_offs[:, None] * stride_kvt + pid_hkv * stride_kvh) k = tl.load(base + d_offs[None, :], mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) v = tl.load(base + (D + d_offs[None, :]), mask=token_mask[:, None], other=0.0) scores = tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)) * SCALE scores = tl.where(token_mask[None, :], scores, -float('inf')) m_new = tl.maximum(m_i, tl.max(scores, axis=1)) alpha = tl.exp(m_i - m_new) p_block = tl.exp(scores - m_new[:, None]) l_i = l_i * alpha + tl.sum(p_block, axis=1) acc = acc * alpha[:, None] + tl.dot(p_block.to(v.dtype), v) m_i = m_new # Write partials (m=-inf, l=0, acc=0 if no pages, otherwise accumulated values) g_offs = tl.arange(0, G) m_ptrs = M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh + pid_split * stride_ms + g_offs l_ptrs = L_ptr + pid_b * stride_lb + pid_hkv * stride_lh + pid_split * stride_ls + g_offs tl.store(m_ptrs, m_i) tl.store(l_ptrs, l_i) acc_ptrs = (ACC_ptr + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_hkv * stride_acch + pid_split * stride_accs + g_offs[:, None] * D + d_offs[None, :]) tl.store(acc_ptrs, acc) @triton.jit def _paged_decode_reduce_kernel( M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr, OUT_ptr, stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms, stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs, stride_ob, stride_oh, G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) g_offs = tl.arange(0, G) s_offs = tl.arange(0, NUM_SPLITS) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) # Load m, l for all splits m_ptrs = M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh + s_offs * stride_ms + g_offs[:, None] # Wait, need to broadcast correctly # m shape: (G, NUM_SPLITS) m_ptrs = (M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh + s_offs[None, :] * stride_ms + g_offs[:, None]) l_ptrs = (L_ptr + pid_b * stride_lb + pid_hkv * stride_lh + s_offs[None, :] * stride_ls + g_offs[:, None]) m = tl.load(m_ptrs) # (G, NUM_SPLITS), fp32 l = tl.load(l_ptrs) # (G, NUM_SPLITS), fp32 # Global max m_global = tl.max(m, axis=1) # (G,) # Re-scale each split and accumulate alpha = tl.exp(m - m_global[:, None]) # (G, NUM_SPLITS) l_new = tl.sum(l * alpha, axis=1) # (G,) # Load acc for all splits and combine # acc shape: (G, NUM_SPLITS, D) acc_ptrs = (ACC_ptr + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_hkv * stride_acch + s_offs[None, :, None] * stride_accs + g_offs[:, None, None] * D + d_offs[None, None, :]) acc = tl.load(acc_ptrs) # (G, NUM_SPLITS, D) # Combine: acc_combined = sum_s (acc[s] * l[s] * alpha[s]) / l_new # Wait, the standard formula: # acc_combined = sum_s (alpha[s] * l[s] * acc[s] / l_new) # Because acc[s] is the weighted output of split s, but it's not normalized # We need: output = sum_s (alpha[s] * l[s] * acc[s]) / l_new # Wait no, let me re-derive. # In each split, acc[s] = sum_l p_block * V (un-normalized) # and l[s] = sum_l p_block (the sum of un-normalized probabilities) # So the normalized output of split s would be acc[s] / l[s] # The alpha is the rescaling factor for the change in max # Combined output: sum_s (alpha[s] * acc[s]) / sum_s (alpha[s] * l[s]) # = sum_s (alpha[s] * acc[s]) / l_new weighted_acc = acc * alpha[None, :, None] # Hmm, alpha shape is (G, NUM_SPLITS) # Actually alpha should be (G, NUM_SPLITS), and acc is (G, NUM_SPLITS, D) # We want weighted_acc[g, s, d] = alpha[g, s] * acc[g, s, d] weighted_acc = acc * alpha[:, :, None] combined_acc = tl.sum(weighted_acc, axis=1) # (G, D) output = combined_acc / l_new[:, None] out = output.to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty) head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) out_ptrs = (OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh + d_offs[None, :]) tl.store(out_ptrs, out) ``` Hmm, the reduce kernel is a bit complex. Let me also think about whether the reduce kernel can be simplified. Instead of a separate Triton kernel, can we do it in PyTorch? Reduce in PyTorch: ```python m_global = m_partial.amax(dim=2) # (B, Hkv, G) alpha = (m_partial - m_global.unsqueeze(2)).exp() # (B, Hkv, NUM_SPLITS, G) l_weighted = l_partial * alpha # (B, Hkv, NUM_SPLITS, G) l_new = l_weighted.sum(dim=2) # (B, Hkv, G) acc_weighted = acc_partial * alpha.unsqueeze(-1) # (B, Hkv, NUM_SPLITS, G, D) acc_combined = acc_weighted.sum(dim=2) # (B, Hkv, G, D) out = (acc_combined / l_new.unsqueeze(-1)).to(query.dtype) ``` This is straightforward but has multiple kernel launches. Acc is also always written, but in the reduce step, we sum all partials. If a split has no work, its acc=0 contribution is fine. So we can use torch.empty for everything. But for safety, let's use torch.zeros for l and acc (we want l=0 and acc=0 for empty splits, and the kernel writes these directly anyway). For m, we want -inf for empty splits. The kernel always writes m, so we can use torch.empty. Hmm wait, in the current code, for non-empty splits, the kernel writes m_i at the end. For empty splits, the kernel still writes m_i (which is -inf initially). So m is always written. OK. Let me code this up. I'll keep PAGES_PER_SPLIT as a constexpr and pre-compute NUM_SPLITS at host time. Let me think about the heuristic once more. We have: - 3090 has 82 SMs - Each SM can have multiple resident blocks (up to 16-32) - For memory-bound kernels, occupancy matters for hiding latency - Aim for at least 4-8 blocks per SM = 328-656 blocks For the shapes: - Shape 0: B=8, Hkv=8 -> 64 base blocks. Need 5-10x splits. - Shape 1: B=32, Hkv=8 -> 256 base blocks. Need 1.5-3x splits. - Shape 2: B=4, Hkv=8 -> 32 base blocks. Need 10-20x splits. - Shape 3: B=16, Hkv=8 -> 128 base blocks. Need 2.5-5x splits. - Shape 4: B=8, Hkv=4 -> 32 base blocks. Need 10-20x splits. Let me use a heuristic: - target_blocks = 4 * 82 = 328 (conservative) - num_splits = max(1, ceil(target_blocks / (B * Hkv))) - PAGES_PER_SPLIT = ceil(num_pages / num_splits), rounded to power of 2 For shape 0: num_splits = ceil(328/64) = 6. pages_per_split = ceil(64/6) = 11, round to 16. For shape 1: num_splits = ceil(328/256) = 2. pages_per_split = ceil(128/2) = 64, round to 64. For shape 2: num_splits = ceil(328/32) = 11. pages_per_split = ceil(256/11) = 24, round to 32. For shape 3: num_splits = ceil(328/128) = 3. pages_per_split = ceil(96/3) = 32, round to 32. For shape 4: num_splits = ceil(328/32) = 11. pages_per_split = ceil(125/11) = 12, round to 16. PAGES_PER_SPLIT values: 16, 64, 32, 32, 16. This is fine. Let me code it. Wait, there's an issue. PAGES_PER_SPLIT=64 for shape 1 means 64 pages per split. With page_size=16, that's 1024 tokens per split. The split kernel does 64 iterations of loading K and V (each (16, 128)). That's a lot of registers and shared memory. For shape 1, the per-iteration K is (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB. 64 iterations = 256KB if all in registers, but Triton reuses memory so it's just 4KB in registers at a time. The loop is unrolled or pipelined by Triton. With num_stages=2, it should pipeline nicely. Let me also think about register pressure. For shape 1: G=4, D=128, P=16. - Q: (4, 128) bf16 = 1KB - K: (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB - V: (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB - scores: (4, 16) fp32 = 256B - p_block: (4, 16) fp32 = 256B - m_i, l_i: small - acc: (4, 128) fp32 = 2KB Total per-block register usage: ~12KB. With 1 warp = 32 threads, that's 12KB / 32 = 384 bytes per thread = 96 fp32 registers. Within budget. For shape 2 with G=8, D=128: - Q: (8, 128) bf16 = 2KB - K: (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB - V: (16, 128) bf16 = 4KB - scores: (8, 16) fp32 = 512B - p_block: (8, 16) fp32 = 512B - acc: (8, 128) fp32 = 4KB Total: ~15KB. 1 warp = 32 threads, 15KB/32 = 480 bytes = 120 fp32 registers. OK. OK let me write the kernel. Hmm wait, for the reduce kernel, we need to load all partials. For NUM_SPLITS=32, that's loading 32 * G * D fp32 values. The acc partial is (NUM_SPLITS, G, D) = (32, 8, 128) = 32K elements * 4B = 128KB per (b, hkv). That's a lot to load in registers. We can't hold it all in registers. We need to process splits one at a time and accumulate. OK let me think about the reduce algorithm differently. We have: - m[s], l[s] for each split s - acc[s] = un-normalized weighted output of split s We want: - m_global = max_s m[s] - l_combined = sum_s l[s] * exp(m[s] - m_global) - acc_combined = sum_s acc[s] * exp(m[s] - m_global) - output = acc_combined / l_combined We can process splits one at a time: ```python m_global = -inf l_combined = 0 acc_combined = 0 for s in 0..NUM_SPLITS: m_s = m_partial[s] l_s = l_partial[s] acc_s = acc_partial[s] # shape (G, D) m_new = max(m_global, m_s) alpha = exp(m_global - m_new) # rescale factor beta = exp(m_s - m_new) # new contribution factor l_combined = alpha * l_combined + beta * l_s acc_combined = alpha * acc_combined + beta * acc_s m_global = m_new output = acc_combined / l_combined ``` This is the standard FlashAttention log-sum-exp combination algorithm. We process splits one at a time, keeping running stats. The acc and l are (G,) and (G, D) shapes - small enough to hold in registers. This way the reduce kernel doesn't need to load all partials at once. Let me code this. ```python @triton.jit def _paged_decode_reduce_kernel( M_ptr, L_ptr, ACC_ptr, OUT_ptr, stride_mb, stride_mh, stride_ms, stride_lb, stride_lh, stride_ls, stride_accb, stride_acch, stride_accs, stride_ob, stride_oh, SCALE: tl.constexpr, # not needed for reduce G: tl.constexpr, D: tl.constexpr, NUM_SPLITS: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1) g_offs = tl.arange(0, G) d_offs = tl.arange(0, D) # Initialize m_global = tl.full((G,), -float('inf'), dtype=tl.float32) l_combined = tl.zeros((G,), dtype=tl.float32) acc_combined = tl.zeros((G, D), dtype=tl.float32) for s in range(NUM_SPLITS): # Load m, l for this split m_ptr = M_ptr + pid_b * stride_mb + pid_hkv * stride_mh + s * stride_ms + g_offs l_ptr = L_ptr + pid_b * stride_lb + pid_hkv * stride_lh + s * stride_ls + g_offs m_s = tl.load(m_ptr) # (G,) l_s = tl.load(l_ptr) # (G,) # Load acc for this split acc_ptr = (ACC_ptr + pid_b * stride_accb + pid_hkv * stride_acch + s * stride_accs + g_offs[:, None] * D + d_offs[None, :]) acc_s = tl.load(acc_ptr) # (G, D) # Combine m_new = tl.maximum(m_global, m_s) alpha = tl.exp(m_global - m_new) beta = tl.exp(m_s - m_new) l_combined = alpha * l_combined + beta * l_s acc_combined = alpha[:, None] * acc_combined + beta[:, None] * acc_s m_global = m_new # Final output output = acc_combined / l_combined[:, None] out = output.to(OUT_ptr.dtype.element_ty) head_offs = pid_hkv * G + tl.arange(0, G) out_ptr = (OUT_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + head_offs[:, None] * stride_oh + d_offs[None, :]) tl.store(out_ptr, out) ``` This is cleaner. Let me put it all together. Wait, I want to double-check the math. In the standard online softmax combination: - m_new = max(m_old, m_new_chunk) - l_new = exp(m_old - m_new) * l_old + exp(m_chunk - m_new) * l_chunk - acc_new = exp(m_old - m_new) * acc_old + exp(m_chunk - m_new) * acc_chunk In my code: - alpha = exp(m_global - m_new), this is the rescale for the old values - beta = exp(m_s - m_new), this is the rescale for the new chunk So: - l_combined = alpha * l_combined + beta * l_s ✓ - acc_combined = alpha * acc_combined + beta * acc_s ✓ OK that's correct.  """Paged attention decode kernel (Triton) for SM86 (RTX 3090).
 
-Single-program per (batch, kv_head) approach:
-  - Grid: (B, Hkv) programs
-  - Each program handles all G=num_heads/num_kv_heads query heads sharing one
-    kv_head (GQA).
-  - Iterates over pages of the block_table, applies online softmax
-    (FlashAttention-style streaming) and accumulates output in fp32.
-  - Memory-bound: the workload streams the KV cache from HBM.
+Two-stage FlashDecoding approach for high SM utilization on small batches:
+  Stage 1 (split): each (batch, kv_head, split) program processes a chunk of
+                   pages for that kv_head and writes partial (m, l, acc).
+  Stage 2 (reduce): combine splits per (batch, kv_head) into the final output.
+
+Memory-bound; the workload is dominated by streaming the KV cache from HBM.

When 32 threads in a warp load 128 bf16 elements, they each load 4 bf16 = 8 bytes. With coalesced access, 32 threads load 32*8 = 256 bytes in one transaction. But 256 bytes is 2 cache lines (128 bytes each). The GPU issues 2 transactions per warp. For the 16 pages, we have 16 K loads of 256 bytes each = 16 * 2 = 32 transactions per block. Triton's tl.dot needs to handle the transposed access. In Triton, tl.dot can handle transposed access via shared memory layout. But the transpose might add overhead. Alternative: load K transposed as (D, P) directly. This requires loading with strides such that consecutive memory addresses are along the P dimension for a fixed d, which means strided access in memory (since the natural layout is (P, D)). For (D, P) load: for d, t: offset d * stride_p_in_memory + t. With the natural layout (P, D) where stride_p = D, stride_d = 1, the offset for (d, t) is d + t * D. This is the same as the natural access for (t, d), just with the indexing swapped. So it's a strided access. Triton can handle this. The question is whether it's faster than the transpose in shared memory. Let me try this approach. Actually wait, there's another approach. We can compute scores in chunks along the D dimension. import torch
import reference
import solution
B, H, Hkv, D, L, P = 8, 32, 8, 128, 1024, 16
reference.BATCH = B; reference.NUM_HEADS = H; reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = Hkv
reference.HEAD_DIM = D; reference.SEQ_LEN = L; reference.PAGE_SIZE = P
init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()
ref = reference.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
sol = solution.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
torch.manual_seed(42)
inputs = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
# Warmup
for _ in range(3):
    sol(*inputs)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
out = sol(*inputs)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
print('done', out.shape)

#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
name="$1"
real="$2"
shift 2
if [ -z "$real" ]; then
    echo "$name is unavailable" >&2
    exit 127
fi
real_abs="$(readlink -f "$real" 2>/dev/null || printf '%s' "$real")"
case "$name" in
    uv)
        fallback="${REAL_UV_FALLBACK:-}"
        ;;
    python|python3)
        fallback="${REAL_PYTHON_FALLBACK:-}"
        ;;
    *)
        fallback=""
        ;;
esac
if [ -n "${RUN_DIR:-}" ] && [[ "$real_abs" == "${RUN_DIR}/bin/"* ]] && [ -n "$fallback" ]; then
    real="$fallback"
fi
if [ "${KBH_GPU_LOCK_HELD:-0}" = "1" ]; then
    exec "$real" "$@"
fi
if [ "${KBH_AGENT_PHASE:-0}" = "1" ]; then
    case "$name" in
        uv|python|python3|nvidia-smi|nvcc)
            exec "$real" "$@"
            ;;
        ncu|nsys)
            echo "$name is disabled during KernelBench parallel agent phase; official benchmarking runs under the GPU lock after generation." >&2
            exit 125
            ;;
    esac
fi
owner_file="${KBH_GPU_LOCK}.owner"
if [ -f "$owner_file" ]; then
    IFS=$'\t' read -r owner_pid owner_run_dir < "$owner_file" || true
    if [ "${owner_run_dir:-}" = "${RUN_DIR:-}" ] && kill -0 "${owner_pid:-}" 2>/dev/null; then
        exec "$real" "$@"
    fi
fi
{
    printf '%s wait pid=%s cmd=%s args=%q\n' "$(date -Is)" "$$" "$name" "$*" >&3
    lock_wait_timeout="${KBH_GPU_LOCK_WAIT_TIMEOUT_SECONDS:-}"
    if [ -n "$lock_wait_timeout" ] && [ "$lock_wait_timeout" != "0" ]; then
        if ! flock -x -w "$lock_wait_timeout" 9; then

For P=16, D=128, the load is 16 separate strided loads of 128 bf16 each. For 32 threads in a warp: - 16 rows (tokens), 128 cols (D) - Each thread handles 16*128/32 = 64 elements - 4 elements per thread per row, 16 rows = 64 elements per thread Wait, in Triton, the load is typically vectorized. The compiler decides how to map threads to data. For (16, 128) = 2048 elements, with 32 threads, each thread loads 64 elements. The vectorization can be: - Each thread loads 4 bf16 = 8 bytes per "transaction" - 2048 / 32 = 64 elements = 16 transactions of 4 elements each The stride is stride_kvt = 2048 elements = 4096 bytes. So consecutive transactions (within a thread) access different rows. The stride between rows is 4096 bytes. In terms of memory access pattern: - 32 threads load 4 bf16 each, total 256 bytes per warp transaction - Then 32 threads load the next 4 bf16 each, total 256 bytes - The 16 rows are at 4096-byte intervals This is somewhat strided. The GPU handles this via caching. L1/L2 cache lines are 128 bytes, so 256 bytes spans 2 cache lines. For 16 rows, the warp issues 16 separate 256-byte loads. Each is 2 cache lines. So 32 cache line accesses per warp per K load. If the warp's accesses hit L2, this is fast. If they hit HBM, this is the bottleneck. For shape 0: 64 K pages per (b, hkv), 64 (b, hkv) pairs. Total = 64 * 64 * 16 = 65536 K row-loads. Each is 256 bytes = 16MB. Plus V is the same = 16MB. Total 32MB. But the bf16 sizes for the data are 16.78MB (KV) + small (Q, Out). cat > /tmp/tune_paged.py << 'EOF'
import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_183353_minimax-claude_MiniMax-M3_03_paged_attention/repo/problems/03_paged_attention')
import torch
import reference
import solution
import math

def time_shape(B, H, Hkv, D, L, P, n_warmup=5, n_iter=30):
    reference.BATCH = B; reference.NUM_HEADS = H; reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = Hkv
    reference.HEAD_DIM = D; reference.SEQ_LEN = L; reference.PAGE_SIZE = P
    init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()
    sol = solution.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
    torch.manual_seed(42)
    inputs = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
    for _ in range(n_warmup):
        sol(*inputs)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    times = []
    for _ in range(n_iter):
        torch.cuda.synchronize()
        s = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
        e = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)
        s.record()
        sol(*inputs)
        e.record()
        torch.cuda.synchronize()
        times.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    times.sort()
    median = times[len(times)//2]
    return median, sol

shapes = [
    (8, 32, 8, 128, 1024, 16),
    (32, 32, 8, 128, 2048, 16),
    (4, 64, 8, 128, 4096, 16),
    (16, 32, 8, 128, 1535, 16),
    (8, 16, 4, 64, 2000, 16),
]
for shape in shapes:
    median, sol = time_shape(*shape)
    bytes_moved = 2 * shape[0] * shape[4] * shape[2] * shape[3] * 2 + shape[0] * shape[1] * shape[3] * 2 * 2
    gbps = bytes_moved / median / 1000
    print(f'shape {shape}: pps={sol.pages_per_split} ns={sol.num_splits} t={median*1000:.1f}us gbps={gbps:.1f}')
EOF

1	"""Paged attention decode kernel (Triton) for SM86 (RTX 3090).
2	
3	Two-stage FlashDecoding approach for high SM utilization on small batches:
4	  Stage 1 (split): each (batch, kv_head, split) program processes a chunk of
5	                   pages for that kv_head and writes partial (m, l, acc).
6	  Stage 2 (reduce): combine splits per (batch, kv_head) into the final output.
7	
8	Memory-bound; the workload is dominated by streaming the KV cache from HBM.
9	"""

Per block (16 pages): 64KB of K + 64KB of V = 128KB. Hmm, the per-block work is small. Maybe combining more pages per block helps. Actually let me think about this. For shape 4: - 32 (b, hkv) blocks - 125 pages per (b, hkv) - With PAGES_PER_SPLIT=16, 8 splits, 256 total blocks - Per block: 16 iterations of 4KB loads If I increase PAGES_PER_SPLIT to 32: 4 splits, 128 blocks, 32 iter per block. Half the blocks, double the work per block. If I decrease to 8: 16 splits, 512 blocks, 8 iter per block. Let me just try different values. Actually, you know what, let me also reconsider the entire approach. Maybe the issue is the K|V access pattern. The K cache is stored as (num_blocks, P, Hkv, 2*D). For a fixed (block, hkv), the K data is (P, D) = 16*128 = 2048 bf16 = 4KB. The data is NOT contiguous in memory because of the Hkv and 2D dimensions. For one block, the K layout is: - 16 tokens, each 128 bf16 - Each token at offset 0, 2048, 4096, ..., 30720 (in bf16 elements) - Within a token: 128 bf16 contiguous So 16 strided loads of 256 bytes each. If I instead load multiple pages at once, I could: - For PAGES_PER_SPLIT=4 pages: 4 pages = 64 tokens. 64 strided loads of 256 bytes each. - For PAGES_PER_SPLIT=1 page: 1 page = 16 tokens. 16 strided loads. The stride is the same (2048 elements = 4096 bytes). The number of loads varies. What if I load a larger tile that spans multiple pages? Like (PAGES_PER_SPLIT * P, D) = (256, 128) for PAGES_PER_SPLIT=16. This would be one big strided load. Hmm but the stride between tokens is 2048, not 1. The load would still be strided. Actually the issue is: tokens within a page are at offset 0, 2048, 4096, ..., 30720. Across pages, the offset is page_id * 32768 + t * 2048 + hkv * 256. So consecutive tokens (across page boundary) are at offset ... + 30720, then 32768 + 0 + 256 = 33024. The gap is 2304 elements. So tokens are NEVER adjacent in memory. The minimum stride is 2048 (within a page). To make the load more efficient, we'd need to gather tokens into shared memory or use a different access pattern. This is what vLLM/FlashInfer do: they have a "split-KV" cache layout where K is contiguous. But for our problem, the cache layout is fixed. We can't change it. OK so we're stuck with the strided access. The question is how to make it efficient. In Triton, the compiler should handle the strided access. The load becomes a series of memory accesses at strided locations. The L1/L2 cache should handle the rest. The achieved 522 GB/s for shape 0 (52% of peak) is decent but not great. Can we do better? Let me try the combined K|V load. This doubles the row size from 256 bytes to 512 bytes, but keeps the same number of rows. The advantage is fewer memory transactions (1 per row instead of 2). Actually, I realize the K and V loads for the same token are adjacent in memory. If we issue them as a single 512-byte load, the GPU can do it in 4 cache line accesses (vs 4 for K + 4 for V = 8 if separate). But the GPU's L1/L2 cache might already combine these. Hmm let me just try. Also, let me try a smaller per-iteration chunk. Instead of (P, D) = (16, 128), try (P, D) = (16, 64) with two iterations per page. Or some other chunking. Actually, a better idea: what if we use a different parallelization scheme? Instead of one block per (b, hkv), use one block per (b, hkv, page)? For shape 0: 64 (b, hkv) * 64 pages = 4096 blocks. Each block does 1 page. This gives massive parallelism but more blocks means more launch overhead. Hmm, 4096 blocks might be too many. Let me think. OK let me just try things and measure.
